<div id="review_230412019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230412019" />
    <a title="Fraffee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3514917-fraffee"><img alt="Fraffee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468797164p2/3514917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230412019?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fraffee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fraffee" href="/user/show/3514917-fraffee">Fraffee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061955044" href="/book/show/7289934-the-gift">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fraffee by: </span>
      My wonderful English teacher's DEAR reading list
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230412019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3486442942063892242">This book truly stuck a nerve and one of my heart strings at the same time. After reading the book, I was put in a state of shock. But it was a good kind of shock. If you were to ask me if this book changed my life then I would say that in a way, it did. Don't misunderstand me, though. This book did not turn my world upside down and left me breathless. But what it really did was even more amazing. It opened my eyes.<br/><br/>I can confidently say that Cecelia Ahern is a gifted writer. To be honest, I had </span>
  <span id="freeText3486442942063892242" style="display:none">This book truly stuck a nerve and one of my heart strings at the same time. After reading the book, I was put in a state of shock. But it was a good kind of shock. If you were to ask me if this book changed my life then I would say that in a way, it did. Don't misunderstand me, though. This book did not turn my world upside down and left me breathless. But what it really did was even more amazing. It opened my eyes.<br /><br />I can confidently say that Cecelia Ahern is a gifted writer. To be honest, I had a hard time adjusting to her writing style at first. But as I got more into the story, I found her writing to be simply beautiful. She writes with so much emotion and passion; therefore, her characters came across as real people. <br /><br />Lou Suffern frustrated me many times in the book. He can be a real prick sometimes but I do not and cannot doubt his love for his family. It may not seem evident in the book to some but I realized at the end that he loved his wife and family more than he even realized. I also liked Gabe. And it is one of my theories that he is in fact an angel sent from Heaven - his name, Gabe, which is short for Gabriel, was a total giveaway. I grew fond of so many characters - though their roles may seem miniscule - and I think that's because Cecelia Ahern wrote them so well. In a funny way, I also cannot forget Smug Family Man - reading about him made me laugh. <br /><br />The greatest thing about the book that cannot be overlooked is the message it gave me. It presented the lesson we all hear and know. It presented the lesson we are told time and time again - but I observed that we never seemed to absorb it. <br /><br />Time is precious. Money can always be reproduced - it's just paper after all. Diamonds and rubies can be overlooked - they're just mostly for jewelry anyway. But like what the book said, Time cannot be made or given. <br /><br />That message hit me cold and hard in the face this time. I believe that this book meant more for me than most people because in a way, I am like Lou Suffern. I am a workaholic and a study addict. I probably spend more time in my room studying than actually living. I even put all my assignments above simple family matters. And what am I doing it all for? An award? Recognition from my peers?<br /><br />This book also made me realize that there IS more to life than pleasing people and pleasing yourself - because at the end of the day and at the end of your life, none of your achievements will even matter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3486442942063892242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Io4YI+2QRS74xlls/7B65nwNfeQcxTRe/yWpqoXk2CAT48MM4pMPMN67hCylmv52Dz/fK3Nhk62p2yJeUiQxzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vbOWgWdqI6nGsgMGMOi7ek30E89ErwnFqnvMTmfjUbaM3k2uaGlpt+DP3kZqwj/qPsaxACsLrjb8hUe6sCO4Ww==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44542253-the-invisible-man"><img alt="The Invisible Man : H G Wells" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1553040794l/44542253._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_44542253'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44542253-the-invisible-man?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Invisible Man : H G Wells<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/9573.Michael_Coren?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Michael Coren<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.19 avg rating &mdash; 95 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published \n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer16027478228471766995\">For almost half a century H. G. Wells was an international phenomenon, the only writer of his time who could command an audience with both Roosevelt and Stalin.  His circle of friends included George Bernard Shaw, Rudyard Kipling, G. K. Chesterton, S<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16027478228471766995\" style=\"display:none\">For almost half a century H. G. Wells was an international phenomenon, the only writer of his time who could command an audience with both Roosevelt and Stalin.  His circle of friends included George Bernard Shaw, Rudyard Kipling, G. K. Chesterton, Somerset Maugham and, of course, the young Rebecca West, with whom he had a long-term affair — perhaps the most tempestuous and sparkling literary liaison of the century. Equally illustrious was his circle of enemies, including the indomitable Hilaire Belloc, who destroyed Wells in a vicious and public argument.  Unlike any previous biographer, Michael Coren shows that while many have considered Wells to be on the side of the angels, he was in fact invariably on the wrong side in the major political and literary debates of the age.  Drawing on eye-opening new material, The Invisible Man delves deep into the paradoxes that characterized Wells — the utopian visionary and staunch advocate of women’s suffrage who was also a misogynistic womanizer; the epitome of liberal tolerance who was also a social engineer and thoroughgoing anti-Semite.  Wells has hitherto remained untouched by charges of anti-Semitism, but Coren reveals for the first time his disturbing views on ‘the Jewish problem’ (for instance, he called Jews ‘termites in the civilized world’), views he defended vehemently even through the 1930s.  The avuncular author of Kipps and The Time Machine is depicted, shockingly, as one who advocated concentration camps, racial eugenics and the incarceration or execution of those who did not ‘fit in’. The Invisible Man is one of those iconoclastic biographies that change our perception of their subjects for ever.   Praise for Michael Coren: ‘An elegantly written biography’ The Times  Michael Coren is a journalist and author, who wrote the highly acclaimed Gilbert: The Man Who Was G. K. Chesterton and a biography of Sir Arthur Conan Doyle.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16027478228471766995\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern">About Cecelia Ahern</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1596427608p3/7116.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern">Cecelia Ahern
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
16,403
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6560102698148391376">Cecelia Ahern was born and grew up in Dublin. She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>

</div>
</div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Time cant be given. But it can be shared.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;There was a magic about the sea. People were drawn to it. People wanted to love by it, swim in it, play in it, look at it. It was a living thing that as as unpredictable as a great stage actor: it could be calm and welcoming, opening its arms to embrace it's audience one moment, but then could explode with its stormy tempers, flinging people around, wanting them out, attacking coastlines, breaking down islands. It had a playful side too, as it enjoyed the crowd, tossed the children about, knocked lilos over, tipped over windsurfers, occasionally gave sailors helping hands; all done with a secret little chuckle&rdquo;</span>
